  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_80131fd8-884d-40e1-a21d-3c17230b0f5e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1111939906?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1111939906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14199381939651623927">This really grew on me. It had to. I started the book frustrated with Barbara, with her disconnect from the real world and total immersion in a fantasy world she's created, with her near inability to interact with the people around her. That's a bold thing that Kelly did, to start the reader off with an entirely outside perspective of Barbara, and only slowly reveal exactly what is going on inside her heart and mind, and what events in her life have caused her to react in this way. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler</a></span>
  <span id="freeText14199381939651623927" style="display:none">This really grew on me. It had to. I started the book frustrated with Barbara, with her disconnect from the real world and total immersion in a fantasy world she's created, with her near inability to interact with the people around her. That's a bold thing that Kelly did, to start the reader off with an entirely outside perspective of Barbara, and only slowly reveal exactly what is going on inside her heart and mind, and what events in her life have caused her to react in this way. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Her mother is dying of cancer, and Barbara refuses to accept that. Her giant killing fantasy is the way she's tried to construct an actual, material thing she can do to save her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Once I understood her, and even earlier, when I was just beginning to see that there was something to understand, I became entirely absorbed in her story. In the end, this turned out to be a surprisingly moving and heart-felt story, and I'm very, very glad that I read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14199381939651623927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_655724537" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/655724537" />
    <a title="Ronyell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell"><img alt="Ronyell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506581787p2/1169488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/655724537?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronyell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronyell" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell">Ronyell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Giants and stories that hit home!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=graphic-novels-comics">graphic-novels-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=image-comics">image-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=modern-age-comics">modern-age-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=joe-kelly">joe-kelly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=strong-heroine">strong-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer655724537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16546567088946070994"> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380427458i/854547._SY540_.jpg' width='300' height='400' alt='I Kill Giants' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>5.5 stars!</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Introduction:</u>
</b> <br/><br/>I have read so many Image Comics over time (Saga, Invincible, Chew) and I have been enjoying every one of them! Now, I had stumbled upon this unique little comic called “I Kill Giants” which is written by Joe Kelly along with artwork by JM Ken Niimura and it was seriously one of the most creative and intense comics I had ever read!<br/><br/><b>
  <u>What is this story about?</u>
</b> <br/><br/>Barbara Thorson was just your average fifth-grade student…alright maybe not so average student. Barbara’</span>
  <span id="freeText16546567088946070994" style="display:none"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380427458i/854547._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="I Kill Giants" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>5.5 stars!</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <u>Introduction:</u>
</b> <br><br>I have read so many Image Comics over time (Saga, Invincible, Chew) and I have been enjoying every one of them! Now, I had stumbled upon this unique little comic called “I Kill Giants” which is written by Joe Kelly along with artwork by JM Ken Niimura and it was seriously one of the most creative and intense comics I had ever read!<br><br><b>
  <u>What is this story about?</u>
</b> <br><br>Barbara Thorson was just your average fifth-grade student…alright maybe not so average student. Barbara’s big secret is that she kills giants for a living, using her trusty hammer Coveleski! Unfortunately, everyone at school thinks that she is a freak and she seems to have so many personal problems at home. Can Barbara overcome her biggest fear that will allow her to get through life?<br><br><b>
  <u>What I loved about this story:</u>
</b> <br><br><u>Joe Kelly’s writing:</u> Wow! I was just so blown away by Joe Kelly’s emotional yet exciting writing! Honestly, this was the first time I had read any of Joe Kelly’s works and after reading this comic, I am definitely looking forward to reading more of his works! Joe Kelly has done a brilliant job at tying in Barbara’s personal problems with her obsessions with giants as it really brought a true depth to the story. I really wish I could tell you about what Barbara’s personal problems are, but that would pretty much give away the entire plot of this comic, but I will say that you will start tearing up once you hear about Barbara’s fears. I also loved the way that Joe Kelly really delve into why Barbara has such a terrible attitude towards people and why fighting giants has become an obsession to her since even though there were times where I just wanted to yell at Barbara for acting so coldly towards other people, I can actually sympathize with her because she is dealing with a trauma that frightens her. I also loved the mythical references to giants and fairies in this comic, even though they are not too major to the story as they added a fantasy atmosphere to the story.<br><br><u>JM Ken Niimura’s artwork:</u> JM Ken Niimura’s artwork is truly creative and unique to look at, even though there were times where the artwork was a bit scratchy and it was a bit difficult to see what the characters were actually doing in the panels. However, I really loved the way that the characters look slightly cartoonish as it lessens the dark atmosphere of the story a bit. I also loved the black and white colorings of this comic as it really brought in a more serious tone to the story.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380427458i/854548._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="I Kill Giants" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>What made me feel uncomfortable about this story:</u>
</b> <br><br>For anyone who does not like language in comics, this comic does have a bit of language in it, although it is not as strong as some of the more mature comics. Also, this comic is a bit dark, especially with the scenes of Barbara trying to deal with her personal problems.<br><br><b>
  <u>Final Thoughts:</u>
</b> <br><br>Overall, “I Kill Giants” is definitely one comic book that really surprised me! When I looked at the title, I actually thought that this book was going to be a blood fest of the main character slaying giants, but read this comic and the story is much deeper than that and that is what I really loved about this comic! I would <b>HIGHLY RECOMMEND</b> this comic book to absolutely anyone!<br><br><b>Review is also on: <a href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2013/07/i-kill-giants-by-joe-kelly.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></b><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16546567088946070994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1391699902" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1391699902" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4255477-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398251387p2/4255477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1391699902?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/4255477-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1391699902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13487558940746072432"><b>Content warnings:</b><br/>Abelist slurs<br/>Lesbian slurs<br/>Bullying<br/>Violent responses/reactions to non-violent situations<br/><br/>Barbara is a character that I continuously had to remind myself to not judge too harshly. I figured there had to be an explanation. And there is...I'm just not sure it's enough. She's not nice, she's abusive and mean, and there's nothing in these pages that excuses that behavior - though many people make excuses for her behavior. However, there are <em>reasons</em> for her actions, too. It doesn't make</span>
  <span id="freeText13487558940746072432" style="display:none"><b>Content warnings:</b><br>Abelist slurs<br>Lesbian slurs<br>Bullying<br>Violent responses/reactions to non-violent situations<br><br>Barbara is a character that I continuously had to remind myself to not judge too harshly. I figured there had to be an explanation. And there is...I'm just not sure it's enough. She's not nice, she's abusive and mean, and there's nothing in these pages that excuses that behavior - though many people make excuses for her behavior. However, there are <em>reasons</em> for her actions, too. It doesn't make them right, but she's an 11 (or so) year old child and even adults don't always react in the best possible way to difficult circumstances.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461611530i/18888318.jpg" alt="854548-_sx540_sy540_" width="316" height="540" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The author took an interesting angle of not allowing us to know what exactly is going on with Barbara, and not letting us find out until nearly the very end. I went into this book expecting a good fantasy, slaying, giant-killing story. And that's what I got, but on a different level. We, each of us, have giants to slay, things to overcome, and I think children have some of the most difficult ones as they learn how to navigate all the different, and sometimes painful, realities of life.<br><br>So, while I absolutely detested some - or a lot - of the things that Barbara did, it's hard to judge her. Because I understand, too. She takes her pain and anger out on those around her, not always justly, not fairly, but it's an emotional reaction that she can't quite control yet.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1461611530i/18888319._SY540_.jpg" alt="i_kill_giants_pg59" width="477" height="733" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If I could have wished for one thing, it would have been her getting called on the behavior a bit more. The story dealt with getting her to deal with the underlying issue, and that's definitely needed, but I think that if we don't check ourselves when we're in pain and angry, care and empathy can get away from us - and it's a good lesson for kids that might be reading this to learn.<br><br>As I tell my son, nothing excuses violence - and believe me, it's a fine line to walk teaching no violence and the right to defend yourself. That's something I would have appreciated seeing reinforced here. When I started this, in the first dozen or so pages, I was going to pass it on to my daughters' to read. Now, I think I'm going to pass. Because no matter how much I can understand Barbara's pain, I can't excuse her violent responses to non-violent circumstances, or hurtful language - especially in a time when such things are so prevalent as it is.<br><br>There were a couple of things - beyond the violence that I mentioned above - that really bothered me here: 1) the comment from Barbara to her PE teacher (calling the teacher a "bull dyke"), this book would have been much more highly rated. But that's a line I wasn't comfortable with, especially when it was never, ever addressed or recriminated. Honestly, the more I think about it, the madder I get; 2) "fat girl bully"; 3) "I'm not like other girls, other girls are stupid"; 4) the boy/girl interests divide - can we just have a book that shows it's okay to like whatever one wants to like and not disparage others for liking other things? Ugh.<br><br>The more I write my review, the more I dislike what I've read. And that's just the story. I also didn't find the art particularly engaging - most of the time I had a hard time figuring out what was going on. I think that's a stylistic choice to fit with the fantasy/reality divide that we're straddling, but it didn't work for me.<br><br>This review is also available at <a href="https://thebookeaters.net/2016/04/25/review-i-kill-giants/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Eaters</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13487558940746072432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_355449420" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/355449420" />
    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/355449420?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer355449420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13774829164802756940">SPOILERS<br/><br/>Barbara is a pretty headstrong young high school girl who loves Dungeons and Dragons, dislikes school, isn't interested in friends or other people, and is obsessed with giants - more accurately, killing giants. But in our everyday world, is Barbara just a weird kid because we all know giants aren't real. Aren't they...<br/><br/>The most important thing potential readers to this book should understand that it's not a fantasy book (though it contains fantasy elements) and is set in our world, the "r</span>
  <span id="freeText13774829164802756940" style="display:none">SPOILERS<br /><br />Barbara is a pretty headstrong young high school girl who loves Dungeons and Dragons, dislikes school, isn't interested in friends or other people, and is obsessed with giants - more accurately, killing giants. But in our everyday world, is Barbara just a weird kid because we all know giants aren't real. Aren't they...<br /><br />The most important thing potential readers to this book should understand that it's not a fantasy book (though it contains fantasy elements) and is set in our world, the "real world", and that it's far deeper than you'd expect from the manga artwork, macho title, and emo-kid main character. In fact, replace "giant" with "cancer" and you've basically got it.<br /><br />I had such a strong emotional reaction to this book, partly because I knew nothing about it and it unexpectedly caught me off balance, but also because I identified so strongly with Barbara. When I was 12/13 my mum was diagnosed with cancer too and that age is already such a turbulent one that throwing into the mix the hitherto unthinkable possibility of losing your mum suddenly becoming an all-too real inevitability is really hard to deal with. And like Barbara I was also getting my ass kicked on a regular basis by a bully and I found solace not in D&amp;D but in a similar board game called Warhammer (all of which changed within a couple of years, for the better).<br /><br />Writer Joe Kelly and artist JM Ken Nimura bring pathos and heart in portraying Barbara's battle against her own demons through some pretty intense fantasy sequences with the titular giants and by the penultimate chapter when Barbara faces down the Titan I was bawling my eyes out. This comic book has bags of heart and soul in its pages, I can't believe it took me this long to pick it up.<br /><br />Kelly and Nimura tell a difficult story well through an ingenious metaphor of fantasy and the really likeable character of Barbara. Through her inspiring courage and defiance in the face of the void she provides an admirable role model for teens going through parental loss and give them hope for a lighter future. The book goes beyond entertainment and art to illustrate raw human emotion vividly and memorably on the page. "I Kill Giants" is an unforgettable masterpiece that'll touch your spirit and deserves to transcend the audience of comics readers to readers in general. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13774829164802756940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_300742434" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300742434" />
    <a title="Johnathan Morris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7384991-johnathan-morris"><img alt="Johnathan Morris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336770169p2/7384991.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300742434?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johnathan Morris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johnathan Morris" href="/user/show/7384991-johnathan-morris">Johnathan Morris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300742434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7495271387866618544">What an emotional roller coaster! And the first graphic novel to make me cry!<br/><br/>I Kill Giants follows a segment of the life of Barbara Thorsen, arguably the greatest giant slayer of all time, in her quest to defend the world from giants—and maybe defend herself from some giants and ghouls of her own.<br/><br/>Probably my favorite graphic novel, the story opens on the surface with a young, angsty girl trying to follow her passion of bringing down titans and giants. However, as the story progresses we find tha</span>
  <span id="freeText7495271387866618544" style="display:none">What an emotional roller coaster! And the first graphic novel to make me cry!<br /><br />I Kill Giants follows a segment of the life of Barbara Thorsen, arguably the greatest giant slayer of all time, in her quest to defend the world from giants—and maybe defend herself from some giants and ghouls of her own.<br /><br />Probably my favorite graphic novel, the story opens on the surface with a young, angsty girl trying to follow her passion of bringing down titans and giants. However, as the story progresses we find that Barbara and her family are dealing with extra issues out of their control, and that Barbara personally chooses not to tackle. The art of it all was beautifully done in, what I would call, an aesthetically pleasing grunge style.<br /><br />As a teacher, I cannot stress the need for students struggling with great life-altering events to find closure and acceptance in healthy ways. The graphic novel portrays a youth dealing with a hardship in her life the only way she knew how—with her imagination—and readers will find her coping mechanisms both dark and enthralling.<br /><br />Johnathan &amp; Kristin</span>
  <a data-text-id="7495271387866618544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review300742434">

<div id="review_77380040" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77380040" />
    <a title="Seth T." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/160319-seth-t"><img alt="Seth T." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251915636p2/160319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77380040?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seth T." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seth T." href="/user/show/160319-seth-t">Seth T.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/160319-seth-t?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77380040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12252947893340684233">It's good to pick a book with vaulted expectations, set the book down finished an hour and a half later, and have those expectations met. In <i>I Kill Giants</i>' earliest chapters, I was not at all sure this would be the case. The pace felt abrupt, the characterizations suffered some adjacency to verisimilitude, and the ground seemed well-worn and overly familiar as it hadn't been long since I had the pleasure of reading Nate Powell's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2970434.Swallow_Me_Whole' title='Swallow Me Whole by Nate Powell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Swallow Me Whole</a>. Of course, by book's end, all that had been well-</span>
  <span id="freeText12252947893340684233" style="display:none">It's good to pick a book with vaulted expectations, set the book down finished an hour and a half later, and have those expectations met. In <i>I Kill Giants</i>' earliest chapters, I was not at all sure this would be the case. The pace felt abrupt, the characterizations suffered some adjacency to verisimilitude, and the ground seemed well-worn and overly familiar as it hadn't been long since I had the pleasure of reading Nate Powell's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2970434.Swallow_Me_Whole" title="Swallow Me Whole by Nate Powell" rel="nofollow noopener">Swallow Me Whole</a>. Of course, by book's end, all that had been well-enough justified by Kelly and Niimura's wonderful story-telling.<br /><br /><i>I Kill Giants</i> exploits expectations in order to tell a story that, while common, is made special by its telling. The creative team breathes a crisp newness into Barbara Thorson's imaginative life that many such tales lack—and in their lack become shallow caricatures that never come to life for the reader. Traveling with Barbara through the travails of her fifth grader's existence, we are given a unique vantage into the lives and motivations of much of her supporting cast. There are still clichés that never entirely extricate themselves from the narrative weight crushing any spark of life from their shell of an existence(for instance the bully, Taylor, who is just like every other storybook bully you've ever encountered), but for the most part, Kelly's script is a relief.<br /><br />Accordingly, Niimura's visual work shows its excellence by nature of considering just how easy it would have been to really screw up the story by producing the wrong kind of art. When Niimura draws giants, they are impressive. When Niimura draws Barbara the giant slayer, she is awkwardly confident. When Niimura draws the intersection of worlds, we find ourselves charmed or horrified according to how Niimura wants us to feel. The only curiosity that took me out of the story and forced me to wonder at his visual choices was his depiction of Taylor, the bully (yes, her again); despite the character's solidly established age (she's a fifth grader), Niimura draws her as being well-enough into puberty that she's granted <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_B3KdGxEn__U/SX6Kp3vXXgI/AAAAAAAAFsg/_0cXVr1EfOw/s1600-h/IKillGiants5.2.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">heftily developed breasts</a>. While it's not outside the realm of possibility for such a girl to exist (apparently puberty is hitting girls earlier and earlier), it's far enough outside the norm that it may give readers (such as myself) pause.<br /><br />In any case, <i>I Kill Giants</i> is the story of Barbara Thorson. Who kills giants. Or so she tells just about everyone.<br /><br />Barbara is, sigh, precocious and outspoken. She's a bit geek (loves D&amp;D and baseball history) and has a difficult homelife. Her interaction with her teachers (and school psychologist as a result of her interaction with teachers) is less than worthy of emulation. She seems to almost purposely make enemies with those around her. And yet, despite the difficulties she presents for herself and the reader who wants to sympathize, she cuts figure as an able protagonist. She's far from perfect and, for this story at least, we prefer her for it.<br /><br />Amidst portents of the arrival of a grave doom, the heralding of a coming giant, Barbara has to negotiate a society with which she will have nothing to do. Against her wishes, the society around her makes many overtures of peace and goodwill. Some make ground while others break it. And all the while, the unseen world becomes increasingly active as the prophesied doom grows ever nearer. In the end, it's in Barbara's interactions with both worlds and their inevitable clash that <i>I Kill Giants</i>' story takes shape.<br /><br />And it was wonderful to take in.<br /><br />As a final note, it is a happy circumstance that <i>I Kill Giants</i> is as short as it is—for the book certainly bears a second reading (as many things previously hidden are unveiled only with knowledge gained in the book's climax).</span>
  <a data-text-id="12252947893340684233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1540359249" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1540359249" />
    <a title="Liz Janet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5114433-liz-janet"><img alt="Liz Janet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574021381p2/5114433.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1540359249?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz Janet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz Janet" href="/user/show/5114433-liz-janet">Liz Janet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1540359249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6366290320364293080">I got the same feeling with this book that I did with "A Monster Calls", it was good, but not great.<br/>It is the story of a girl named Barbara who thinks she fights giants, the giants being a metaphor for something else of course. Her big sister is taking care of her and her brother, but Barbara does not have the best relationship with them as of late. Something has happened that has distanced them. <br/>It is a very well drawn piece of work, all in black and white. It might have been much better with c</span>
  <span id="freeText6366290320364293080" style="display:none">I got the same feeling with this book that I did with "A Monster Calls", it was good, but not great.<br />It is the story of a girl named Barbara who thinks she fights giants, the giants being a metaphor for something else of course. Her big sister is taking care of her and her brother, but Barbara does not have the best relationship with them as of late. Something has happened that has distanced them. <br />It is a very well drawn piece of work, all in black and white. It might have been much better with coloured pages, but it was not too much missed. I disliked the main character, and the reasons I disliked her, where the same reasons that I understood her actions, because that made what was happening seem all the more real. That is the trait of a good unlikable character, I am glad they got it right. <br />If you liked "A Monster Calls", you will like this, and vice verso, or you will be bored of reading the same thing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6366290320364293080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

I'm not usually a fan of manga-style or black and white artwork but this is great. (Although I do wish there was more black or, at best, a highlight color like red.) I Kill Giants is a surreal allegory (in the style of Joe the Barbarian) about Barbara Thorson, an angsty loner teen who deals with very bad things through fantasy. Or <i>is</i> it fantasy? This coming of age story is also about friendship, courage, bullies, allies, family, and the power of the imagination. Having been a qui</span>
  <span id="freeText11787276164793388057" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480119996i/21276134.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Pretty awesome. I'm not usually a fan of manga-style or black and white artwork but this is great. (Although I do wish there was more black or, at best, a highlight color like red.) I Kill Giants is a surreal allegory (in the style of Joe the Barbarian) about Barbara Thorson, an angsty loner teen who deals with very bad things through fantasy. Or <i>is</i> it fantasy? This coming of age story is also about friendship, courage, bullies, allies, family, and the power of the imagination. Having been a quiet loner in high school, dependent on the catharsis of drawing and writing in notebooks and the escapism of video games, as well as a dark and growing presence in the home, I can totally relate to Barbara's struggle. Worth checking out. </span>

<div id="review_2306561854" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2306561854" />
    <a title="Nicay (dearnicay)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36178759-nicay-dearnicay"><img alt="Nicay (dearnicay)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602162853p2/36178759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2306561854?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicay (dearnicay)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicay (dearnicay)" href="/user/show/36178759-nicay-dearnicay">Nicay (dearnicay)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781632150875" href="/book/show/26527680-i-kill-giants">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2306561854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14147279785497653577">Originally posted @ <a href='https://thenerdysideofaqueen.wordpress.com/2018/02/25/graphic-novel-review-i-kill-giants-by-joe-kelly/' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE NERDY SIDE OF A QUEEN</a><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“You are stronger than you think.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Simple words, yet so deep in giving a meaningful meaning.<br/><br/>I don’t know how I stumble to read this graphic novel, but I remember when I saw my friend reading this, I became intrigued what is the story of it. I Kill Giants is the title and I became curious to find out what is the story all about. Until, I also saw the movie trailer, and I’m shocked that it will be adapted into a movie. That’s why I eagerly read this </span>
  <span id="freeText14147279785497653577" style="display:none">Originally posted @ <a href="https://thenerdysideofaqueen.wordpress.com/2018/02/25/graphic-novel-review-i-kill-giants-by-joe-kelly/" rel="nofollow noopener">THE NERDY SIDE OF A QUEEN</a><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“You are stronger than you think.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Simple words, yet so deep in giving a meaningful meaning.<br /><br />I don’t know how I stumble to read this graphic novel, but I remember when I saw my friend reading this, I became intrigued what is the story of it. I Kill Giants is the title and I became curious to find out what is the story all about. Until, I also saw the movie trailer, and I’m shocked that it will be adapted into a movie. That’s why I eagerly read this and throw all my current readings to devour this one.<br /><br />Barbara Thorson was our main character in the story. Well, she was a little weird, and sometimes mean. She became interested in GIANTS – that she wants to hunt and kill them. Because of being weird, everyone thinks of her as crazy and troublesome because she always went to principal’s office.<br /><br />Everybody doesn’t believe everything Barbara says until she met the giant that would change her perspectives on her life.<br /><br />I Kill Giants was like A Monster’s call graphic novel version, and this time the character was a girl. At first, I don’t know what would be the point of this graphic novel, but until the last pages, I became enthused by the message it wants to convey.<br /><br />Though the character Barbara was weird – in terms of outfit and character, I became attached to her and what she was going through with her life.<br /><br />Few pages, yet it still made my heart ache.<br /><br />Though I hope it became longer because the ending was a little bit fast for me. But overall, the story was very compelling, and I love it to bits! I now know why it is adapted into a movie, and I will surely going to watch it!<br /><br />Very well recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14147279785497653577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6957758432877346270">Whew. I put reading this book off because I knew it was going to wreck me. Reading it a second time, and in one go, was way more gut wrenching. That whole last chapter had me in straight-up tears. <br/><br/>I knew the damn ending and I still cried. <br/><br/>This book sets you up to have fun with some quirks but with a heavy, heavy cloud over head.   <span id="freeText6957758432877346270" style="display:none">Whew. I put reading this book off because I knew it was going to wreck me. Reading it a second time, and in one go, was way more gut wrenching. That whole last chapter had me in straight-up tears. <br /><br />I knew the damn ending and I still cried. <br /><br />This book sets you up to have fun with some quirks but with a heavy, heavy cloud over head. How we get to the end is the most important part, and watching Barbara lose control, chapter after chapter, is the roughest part of the story. You know something bad looms, and yet she somehow tries to persevere with witticisms and, in most cases, lashing out under the guise of "giant killing."<br /><br />I cannot express enough how fantastic of a read this was. Going head-first into this book, not second guessing anything, it is a testament to the fantastic creative delivery made by Joe Kelly and J. M. Ken Niimura's work.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173615999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5391778599088489611">This book is why God or Santa Claus or Alan Moore or whoever invented graphic novels and it's the perfect example of why they are a valid and worthy literary form. The art and text together make the story. It's a truly beautiful collaboration between Joe Kelly and JM Ken Niimura. <br/><br/>This is the story of Long Island fifth grader Barbara Thorson. She is iconoclastic and nearly friendless-until she meets a girl named Sophia and the school guidance counselor. She is a Dungeon Master extraordinaire. She</span>
  <span id="freeText5391778599088489611" style="display:none">This book is why God or Santa Claus or Alan Moore or whoever invented graphic novels and it's the perfect example of why they are a valid and worthy literary form. The art and text together make the story. It's a truly beautiful collaboration between Joe Kelly and JM Ken Niimura. <br /><br />This is the story of Long Island fifth grader Barbara Thorson. She is iconoclastic and nearly friendless-until she meets a girl named Sophia and the school guidance counselor. She is a Dungeon Master extraordinaire. She has great millinery taste. She lives with her brother and older sister. Her dad has flown the coop. Her mother...well, that's the mystery. Something is happening with her mother. And by the way, Barbara claims to kill giants with her magical hammer Coveleski (this quirky, charming bit is a baseball reference that thankfully for me was explained) that she carries in her clutch. She sees fairies and dwarves and harbingers of doom. And she'd no doubt kick my ass for calling her Coveleski pouch a clutch. And I was pretty sure I was in love with her by the first time she gets called to the principal's office. <br /><br />I defy you not to laugh, then cry then laugh and cry. Don't read the last chapter in a public place unless you don't mind people staring at you while you do all of the above. I flat out loved this. </span>

<div id="review_2378787057" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2378787057" />
    <a title="Leah Rachel von Essen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2650868-leah-rachel-von-essen"><img alt="Leah Rachel von Essen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571335941p2/2650868.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2378787057?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah Rachel von Essen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah Rachel von Essen" href="/user/show/2650868-leah-rachel-von-essen">Leah Rachel von Essen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781607069850" href="/book/show/20906545-i-kill-giants">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2650868-leah-rachel-von-essen?shelf=graphic-novels-comics-art">graphic-novels-comics-art</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2378787057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1545988138528473605">I Kill Giants by Joe Kelly, illustrated by JM Ken Nimura, is a stunning and emotionally effective graphic novel about a young girl’s world and the monsters she battles. <br/><br/>Drawn in lush, shadowy black and white, it tells the story of Barbara Thorson, a fifth grader who struggles to make friends and gets bullied quite frequently. She doesn’t have the easiest home life, and she has a rough-and-tough personality that can make her hard to deal with. But the strangest thing about her is also the simples</span>
  <span id="freeText1545988138528473605" style="display:none">I Kill Giants by Joe Kelly, illustrated by JM Ken Nimura, is a stunning and emotionally effective graphic novel about a young girl’s world and the monsters she battles. <br /><br />Drawn in lush, shadowy black and white, it tells the story of Barbara Thorson, a fifth grader who struggles to make friends and gets bullied quite frequently. She doesn’t have the easiest home life, and she has a rough-and-tough personality that can make her hard to deal with. But the strangest thing about her is also the simplest: she kills giants. When a new girl named Sofia moves in nearby, Barbara’s life begins to shift somewhat beneath her feet, and meanwhile the warnings of the giants are growing ever closer. It’s a beautiful graphic novel, and I can’t say too much without spoiling it. I would skip the somewhat pretentious introduction by filmmaker Chris Colombus and dive right in to this simple but stunning fantasy / surrealist story about a young girl just trying to survive her world and find her strengths, about belief, about the power of imagination and what it can do for a young girl who needs to escape. This magical world and its breathtaking climax will speak to the heart of anyone who grew up seeing monsters and friends and a shimmer of magic everywhere they went, and who used their fantasy worlds to escape the harder things in their lives. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1545988138528473605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10333797399617554826">When we are adults we tend to remember our childhood and teenage years as the good old days, we keep sweet memories but no matter how happy we were (and I was a happy child indeed) it was never a piece of a cake. There were hard moments. Surviving school and high school sometimes could get rough. We had problems grown ups considered ridiculous, but they were massive for us. So much for a regular kid, but Barbara's life is somehow not very common: She lives with her sister and her brother. She ki</span>
  <span id="freeText10333797399617554826" style="display:none">When we are adults we tend to remember our childhood and teenage years as the good old days, we keep sweet memories but no matter how happy we were (and I was a happy child indeed) it was never a piece of a cake. There were hard moments. Surviving school and high school sometimes could get rough. We had problems grown ups considered ridiculous, but they were massive for us. So much for a regular kid, but Barbara's life is somehow not very common: She lives with her sister and her brother. She kills giants and she claims to do so very soon in the story. <br /> Barbara is on a mission. She is waiting for the giants to come, at which time she will fend them off with her deadly hammer. Barbara lets everyone who will listen know what she does. She spends all of her time reading books about Giants and keeps her Giant killing Hammer named Coveleski with her at all times. The only problem is, nobody else can see these giants either.<br /><br />Barbara is a tough fifth grader. Not only does she kill giants but she wears giant bunny ears, has regular conversations with fairies, struggles and fights with teachers and pupils alike, even with some bullies. She's the underdog and proud to be so. She is crossed by the behaviour of those who surround her who she considers stupid and annoying, but it's because they can't see what she sees.Only fellow student Sophia manages to crack Barbara's thick shell, insisting to win her friendship - something that no one else ever has--despite how difficult Barbara makes things for her. Because people around her, like the reader spend most of the story wondering if Barbara is just plain crazy, or if there really is something more going on than we can see. Of course, as in every good story, there is something going on underneath the surface. Things are never what they seem and there are always battles to fight.<br />All of us have had to face our own giants and Barbara is so sweet and relatable :) Inspiring </span>
  <a data-text-id="10333797399617554826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1228683012" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1228683012" />
    <a title="Nannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1218912-nannah"><img alt="Nannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507141437p2/1218912.jpg" /></a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218912-nannah?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218912-nannah?shelf=with-illustrations">with-illustrations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218912-nannah?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218912-nannah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1228683012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16296622673972196769">Okay, this graphic novel left me so conflicted I'm not sure even where to begin soooo . . . <br/><br/><b>Book content warnings:</b><br/>ableist slurs <br/>lesbophobic slurs<br/><br/>Basically, this book is about Barbara Thorson, a young girl who "kills giants" both imaginary and real. Sooner or later, though, she's going to have to face her ultimate fear: the Titan.<br/><br/>Only, the titan isn't so imaginary and is something that's all to real to many people (and kids). I won't spoil it for you, but to be honest, the family drama, and this </span>
  <span id="freeText16296622673972196769" style="display:none">Okay, this graphic novel left me so conflicted I'm not sure even where to begin soooo . . . <br /><br /><b>Book content warnings:</b><br />ableist slurs <br />lesbophobic slurs<br /><br />Basically, this book is about Barbara Thorson, a young girl who "kills giants" both imaginary and real. Sooner or later, though, she's going to have to face her ultimate fear: the Titan.<br /><br />Only, the titan isn't so imaginary and is something that's all to real to many people (and kids). I won't spoil it for you, but to be honest, the family drama, and this reality is what I enjoyed. This and the ending, which did fill me up with contented feelings and a smile.<br /><br />But there was so much I didn't like. I get Barbara is dealing with a <i>ton</i>, but to have this child yelling out slurs (that are also an issue with kids? like the "r" word and the "d" lesbian slur) just seemed like overkill. She also had the worst case of the "I'm not like other girls because they're stupid" attitude I've ever seen or read. This thinking needs to die immediately.<br /><br />And then there's the matter of the fact that Joe Kelly can't write girls for shit. Especially young girls. He has no idea what they're like. "It's <b>weird</b> that you like all this <b>boy stuff</b> . . . but it's cool. How do you know about baseball?" says Barbara's friend. <br /><br />??? what. You're right, no girls like baseball. None. Except for Barbara Thorson, apparently. <br /><br />I also groaned when he fell back on the "fat girl bully" stereotype. Can we be done with this already? She was the only fat character in the graphic novel, also. You have to know what you're doing when you so obviously set your cast like that.<br /><br />Soooo, I guess there were a ton more that I disliked than liked. The good just doesn't make reading it worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16296622673972196769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_312237815" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/312237815" />
    <a title="Jean-Paul Bass" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8156116-jean-paul-bass"><img alt="Jean-Paul Bass" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334293588p2/8156116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/312237815?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean-Paul Bass" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean-Paul Bass" href="/user/show/8156116-jean-paul-bass">Jean-Paul Bass</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer312237815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18437515603000702273">I was excited about reading I Kill Giants–the title itself was enough to get my attention. And then I read the description and was even more intrigued. Barbara is a loner, an odd kid, who escapes into a fantasy world to avoid dealing with real life. As the fantasy world starts bleeding into reality, Barbara becomes more and more convinced that something big is coming and it’s her duty to stop it.<br/><br/>Barbara is just enough of a smartass to make you feel sorry for her. A kid who backtalks like her mus</span>
  <span id="freeText18437515603000702273" style="display:none">I was excited about reading I Kill Giants–the title itself was enough to get my attention. And then I read the description and was even more intrigued. Barbara is a loner, an odd kid, who escapes into a fantasy world to avoid dealing with real life. As the fantasy world starts bleeding into reality, Barbara becomes more and more convinced that something big is coming and it’s her duty to stop it.<br /><br />Barbara is just enough of a smartass to make you feel sorry for her. A kid who backtalks like her must be dealing with some major issues, right? And she really is, but it’s not until much later in the book that you realize what exactly is going on. Things and situations are hinted at, but it’s never really clear what is wrong until the final confrontation. And what a confrontation it is: Barbara’s fantasies culminate in one big doozy of a battle that threatens herself and those around her.<br /><br />The fantasy becoming reality is the most interesting, and also the best, part of the story. As other people become affected by Barbara’s fantasies, the story perfectly blends reality and fantasy while keeping it all believable.<br /><br />I was impressed with the final villain, from his true purpose in the story to his overall appearance. Niimura did an excellent job portraying a monster that brings an important message along with tons of doom and gloom.<br /><br />Barbara is definitely a character you want to root for and hug at the same time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18437515603000702273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1166054219" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1166054219" />
    <a title="Brittany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26154285-brittany"><img alt="Brittany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516043423p2/26154285.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1166054219?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittany" href="/user/show/26154285-brittany">Brittany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1166054219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16073673441952394204"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422371818i/13492499.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>***Indie 500 Buddy Read with the Shallow Readers! Indie Publisher this time: Image Comics***<br/><br/>I'll admit: I was more than a little confused in the beginning.I was under the very false impression (because my mind really just made it up) that Barbara fought giants all the time because they were running rampant. I don't know why my brain went in that direction, but it did. So when she was the only one who believed in giants, I was baffled. But then things started making more sense. This isn't just a </span>
  <span id="freeText16073673441952394204" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422371818i/13492499.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>***Indie 500 Buddy Read with the Shallow Readers! Indie Publisher this time: Image Comics***<br><br>I'll admit: I was more than a little confused in the beginning.I was under the very false impression (because my mind really just made it up) that Barbara fought giants all the time because they were running rampant. I don't know why my brain went in that direction, but it did. So when she was the only one who believed in giants, I was baffled. But then things started making more sense. This isn't just a story about bravery and courageousness. It's a tale of friendship and family, of growing up and facing your demons, and of learning to cope with any situation that's thrown at you.<br><br>I am in love with this story.<br><br>When I first opened the book I saw that it was in black and white, and I'll be honest, everything I've read graphic novels wise has been bursting with color. I thought that this would deter my feelings for it. I was wrong. The dialogue and story line are so rich with life and love and hatred that you don't even miss colors after a while. Barbara is just a kid who believes that she's been handed a task, and she's more than willing to complete said task in order to save the world, but more importantly, the people she loves. I wouldn't go as far to say that Barbara is initially a selfless person, because I'd totally be lying. She strictly looks out for herself, doesn't bother with friendships, and thinks her family are off their rockers. But her growth through the story is amazing. Every young girl should read this. And young boys. And grandmas and fathers. Because it resounds in you. <br><br>I had to wait to write this review because I knew I wouldn't be able to do it justice. I also knew that there were a few hidden nuggets of information that are crucial to the story, so that's not why I'm jumping in feet first. All I can say is that there are some characters in here that care so much that your heart literally aches. There are characters in here that are whiny little bitches who act tough but aren't shit compared to real giants. And there's a little girl who learns to depend on the love of others to help her through what could be the hardest time in her life. Ugh. All of the love.<br><br>The only reason this didn't get five stars is because I feel like it took too long to really understand the "world" as Babs was seeing it. There was a lot of explanation needed to see what was going on, and you had to work through a lot of one way conversations to fully grasp everything. I think if Kelly had been a bit more forthcoming with just a few small details to really suck you in from the get go, it would've made five stars easily. BUT DON'T BE DETERRED. READ IT.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16073673441952394204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_133149098" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133149098" />
    <a title="jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/670054-jess"><img alt="jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1229683749p2/670054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/133149098?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jess" href="/user/show/670054-jess">jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/670054-jess?shelf=yaf">yaf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/670054-jess?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/670054-jess?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133149098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9968179366040526985">I read this because: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/interviews/show/563.Felicia_Day' rel='nofollow noopener'>Felicia Day told me to.</a><br/><br/>I brought this home from the library, and finished it within 12 hours. This is a noteworthy feat because I have 18 other books sitting next to my bed. I love each of them more than the one before.<br/><br/>This is a YA graphic novel about Barbara, a middle schoolish-aged girl who is dealing with some serious shit. The ways that kids cope with the difficult things in life consistently amaze me and remind me of what the human spirit is capable of. Joe Kelly captur</span>
  <span id="freeText9968179366040526985" style="display:none">I read this because: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/interviews/show/563.Felicia_Day" rel="nofollow noopener">Felicia Day told me to.</a><br /><br />I brought this home from the library, and finished it within 12 hours. This is a noteworthy feat because I have 18 other books sitting next to my bed. I love each of them more than the one before.<br /><br />This is a YA graphic novel about Barbara, a middle schoolish-aged girl who is dealing with some serious shit. The ways that kids cope with the difficult things in life consistently amaze me and remind me of what the human spirit is capable of. Joe Kelly captured the magic of that in this book. Barbara is dealing with the long, slow death of her mother - this is the most painful issue at the core of the story. The terror of a young person living through the deterioration of their parent is fully alive in these pages. This is not a slow-paced emo book, though. Barbara has other issues - not fitting in at school, being bullied, her older sister's terrible cooking, not having friends, and also bearing the solitary burden of killing giants. <br /><br />Barbara is immersed in the world of killing giants - strategies, magical spells, talismans, weapons, traps, mythology and lore - and she uses the hunt for giants both as an escape from real life and a method of processing her feelings about what is happening. There is plenty about loss, grief, loneliness, terror &amp; struggle, but there is also beautiful triumph and quiet, sad moments that let your heart take a whispery, emotional respite from the action-packed fights with school bullies, the school principal &amp; mythological giants. The author &amp; illustrator did a great job of creating emotional space in the story without losing the tension. The rhythm &amp; pace are fantastic. <br /><br />I love this book. I totally cried.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9968179366040526985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('A1eiMU7H7cY2lD0IMAOG4rDi75HiVQxUuJ855Qq6bdlzwMoFdUomQK7czm2Mnpa54zaVyc/RSxLeQCq5Wy7jCw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dloDuKtnWUPSXFv7YY5FDIFgdVa4lAva09ripmG+GdgGzWuMkOqSxUoUqJ7dE1VX0rQPDpUQTJy1BfH6MCqXCg==')})
  }

</script>
